<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Exercise</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Bodily activity that assists health</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Workout" redirects here. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Exercise_(disambiguation)" title="Exercise (disambiguation)">Exercise (disambiguation)</a> and <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Workout_(disambiguation)" title="Workout (disambiguation)">Workout (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Soldier_running_in_water.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1496" data-file-width="963" decoding="async" height="342" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Soldier_running_in_water.jpg/220px-Soldier_running_in_water.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Soldier_running_in_water.jpg/330px-Soldier_running_in_water.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Soldier_running_in_water.jpg/440px-Soldier_running_in_water.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Soldier_running_in_water.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Running" title="Running">Running</a> in water (aquarunning)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MARIANA_DE_MELO.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2272" data-file-width="1704" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/MARIANA_DE_MELO.JPG/170px-MARIANA_DE_MELO.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/MARIANA_DE_MELO.JPG/255px-MARIANA_DE_MELO.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/MARIANA_DE_MELO.JPG/340px-MARIANA_DE_MELO.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MARIANA_DE_MELO.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Weight_training" title="Weight training">Weight training</a></div></div></div>
<p><b>Exercise</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Human_body" title="Human body">body</a> activity that enhances or maintains <a href="/wiki/Physical_fitness" title="Physical fitness">physical fitness</a> and overall <a href="/wiki/Health" title="Health">health</a> and wellness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p><p>It is performed for various reasons, to aid growth and improve strength, develop <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muscle" title="Muscle">muscles</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardiovascular_system" title="Cardiovascular system">cardiovascular system</a>, hone <a href="/wiki/Sport" title="Sport">athletic</a> skills, <a href="/wiki/Weight_loss" title="Weight loss">weight loss</a> or maintenance, improve health,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> or simply for enjoyment. Many individuals choose to <a href="/wiki/Outdoor_fitness" title="Outdoor fitness">exercise outdoors</a> where they can congregate in groups, socialize, and improve <a href="/wiki/Well-being" title="Well-being">well-being</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Mental_health" title="Mental health">mental health</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fitness_for_Foreigners_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fitness_for_Foreigners-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p><p>In terms of health benefits, the amount of recommended exercise depends upon the goal, the type of exercise, and the age of the person. Even doing a small amount of exercise is healthier than doing none.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-3"><div aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading" class="toc" id="toc" role="navigation"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Classification">Classification</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_Army_51673_aerobathon.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="2100" decoding="async" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/US_Army_51673_aerobathon.jpg/280px-US_Army_51673_aerobathon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/US_Army_51673_aerobathon.jpg/420px-US_Army_51673_aerobathon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/US_Army_51673_aerobathon.jpg/560px-US_Army_51673_aerobathon.jpg 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_Army_51673_aerobathon.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An aerobics exercise instructor in the United States instructs her class</div></div></div>
<p>Physical exercises are generally grouped into three types, depending on the overall effect they have on the human body:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-phy_active_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-phy_active-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Aerobic_exercise" title="Aerobic exercise">Aerobic exercise</a> is any <a href="/wiki/Physical_activity" title="Physical activity">physical activity</a> that uses large muscle groups and causes the body to use more <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">oxygen</a> than it would while resting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-phy_active_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-phy_active-6">[6]</a></sup> The goal of aerobic exercise is to increase <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardiovascular" title="Cardiovascular">cardiovascular</a> <a href="/wiki/Endurance" title="Endurance">endurance</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Examples of aerobic exercise include <a href="/wiki/Running" title="Running">running</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cycling" title="Cycling">cycling</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_swimming" title="Human swimming">swimming</a>, brisk <a href="/wiki/Walking" title="Walking">walking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skipping_rope" title="Skipping rope">skipping rope</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rowing_(sports)" title="Rowing (sports)">rowing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hiking" title="Hiking">hiking</a>, dancing, playing <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Continuous_training" title="Continuous training">continuous training</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Long_slow_distance" title="Long slow distance">long distance</a> running.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-phy_active_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-phy_active-6">[6]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Anaerobic_exercise" title="Anaerobic exercise">Anaerobic exercise</a>, which includes <a href="/wiki/Strength_training" title="Strength training">strength</a> and resistance training, can firm, strengthen, and increase muscle mass, as well as improve bone density, <a href="/wiki/Balance_(ability)" title="Balance (ability)">balance</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Motor_coordination" title="Motor coordination">coordination</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-phy_active_6-3"><a href="#cite_note-phy_active-6">[6]</a></sup> Examples of strength exercises are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Push-ups" title="Push-ups">push-ups</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pull-up_(exercise)" title="Pull-up (exercise)">pull-ups</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lunge_(exercise)" title="Lunge (exercise)">lunges</a>, squats, bench press. Anaerobic exercise also includes <a href="/wiki/Weight_training" title="Weight training">weight training</a>, <a href="/wiki/Functional_training" title="Functional training">functional training</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eccentric_Training" title="Eccentric Training">eccentric training</a>, <a href="/wiki/Interval_training" title="Interval training">interval training</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sprint_(running)" title="Sprint (running)">sprinting</a>, and <a href="/wiki/High-intensity_interval_training" title="High-intensity interval training">high-intensity interval training</a> which increase short-term muscle strength.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-phy_active_6-4"><a href="#cite_note-phy_active-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Flexibility_(anatomy)" title="Flexibility (anatomy)">Flexibility</a> exercises stretch and lengthen <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muscle" title="Muscle">muscles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-phy_active_6-5"><a href="#cite_note-phy_active-6">[6]</a></sup> Activities such as <a href="/wiki/Stretching" title="Stretching">stretching</a> help to improve <a href="/wiki/Joint" title="Joint">joint</a> flexibility and keep muscles limber.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-phy_active_6-6"><a href="#cite_note-phy_active-6">[6]</a></sup> The goal is to improve the <a href="/wiki/Range_of_motion" title="Range of motion">range of motion</a> which can reduce the chance of injury.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-phy_active_6-7"><a href="#cite_note-phy_active-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Physical exercise can also include training that focuses on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Accuracy" title="Accuracy">accuracy</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sport_agility" title="Sport agility">agility</a>, <a href="/wiki/Human_power" title="Human power">power</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Speed" title="Speed">speed</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-crossfit_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-crossfit-10">[10]</a></sup>
</p><p>
Types of exercise can also be classified as dynamic or static. 'Dynamic' exercises such as steady running, tend to produce a lowering of the <a href="/wiki/Diastole" title="Diastole">diastolic</a> blood pressure during exercise, due to the improved blood flow. Conversely, static exercise (such as weight-lifting) can cause the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Systole_(medicine)" title="Systole (medicine)">systolic</a> pressure to rise significantly, albeit transiently, during the performance of the exercise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p><div style="clear:right;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_effects">Health effects</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Exercise_physiology" title="Exercise physiology">Exercise physiology</a></div>
<p>Physical exercise is important for maintaining <a href="/wiki/Physical_fitness" title="Physical fitness">physical fitness</a> and can contribute to maintaining a healthy weight, regulating the digestive system, building and maintaining healthy bone density, muscle strength, and joint mobility, promoting physiological well-being, reducing surgical risks, and strengthening the immune system. Some studies indicate that exercise may increase life expectancy and the overall quality of life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> People who participate in moderate to high levels of physical exercise have a lower mortality rate compared to individuals who by comparison are not physically active.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Moderate levels of exercise have been correlated with preventing aging by reducing inflammatory potential.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The majority of the benefits from exercise are achieved with around 3500 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metabolic_equivalent" title="Metabolic equivalent">metabolic equivalent</a> (MET) minutes per week, with diminishing returns at higher levels of activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BMJ2016_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-BMJ2016-15">[15]</a></sup> For example, climbing stairs 10 minutes, vacuuming 15 minutes, gardening 20 minutes, running 20 minutes, and walking or bicycling for transportation 25 minutes on a daily basis would <i>together</i> achieve about 3000 MET minutes a week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BMJ2016_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-BMJ2016-15">[15]</a></sup> A lack of <a href="/wiki/Physical_activity" title="Physical activity">physical activity</a> causes approximately 6% of the burden of disease from coronary heart disease, 7% of type 2 diabetes, 10% of breast cancer and 10% of colon cancer worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-16">[16]</a></sup> Overall, physical inactivity causes 9% of premature mortality worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fitness">Fitness</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Physical_fitness" title="Physical fitness">Physical fitness</a></div>
<p>Most people can increase fitness by increasing <a href="/wiki/Physical_activity" title="Physical activity">physical activity</a> levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-17">[17]</a></sup> Increases in muscle size from resistance training are primarily determined by diet and testosterone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> This genetic variation in improvement from training is one of the key physiological differences between elite athletes and the larger population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newsci_geddes_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-newsci_geddes-20">[20]</a></sup> There is evidence that exercising in <a href="/wiki/Middle_age" title="Middle age">middle age</a> may lead to better physical ability later in life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p><p>Early motor skills and development is also related to physical activity and performance later in life. Children who are more proficient with motor skills early on are more inclined to be physically active, and thus tend to perform well in sports and have better fitness levels. Early motor proficiency has a positive correlation to childhood physical activity and fitness levels, while less proficiency in motor skills results in a more sedentary lifestyle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup>
</p><p>The type and intensity of physical activity performed may have an effect on a person's fitness level. There is some weak evidence that <a href="/wiki/High-intensity_interval_training" title="High-intensity interval training">high-intensity interval training</a> may improve a person's <a href="/wiki/VO2_max" title="VO2 max">VO2 max</a> slightly more than lower intensity endurance training.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> However, unscientific fitness methods could lead to sports injuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cardiovascular_system">Cardiovascular system</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cardiovascular_fitness" title="Cardiovascular fitness">Cardiovascular fitness</a></div>
<p>The beneficial effect of exercise on the cardiovascular system is well documented. There is a direct correlation between physical inactivity and cardiovascular disease, and physical inactivity is an independent risk factor for the development of <a href="/wiki/Coronary_artery_disease" title="Coronary artery disease">coronary artery disease</a>. Low levels of physical exercise increase the risk of cardiovascular diseases mortality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aha2017_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-aha2017-26">[26]</a></sup>
</p><p>Children who participate in physical exercise experience greater loss of body fat and increased cardiovascular fitness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Studies have shown that academic stress in youth increases the risk of cardiovascular disease in later years; however, these risks can be greatly decreased with regular physical exercise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> There is a dose-response relationship between the amount of exercise performed from approximately <span class="nowrap">700–2000</span> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kcal" title="Kcal">kcal</a> of energy expenditure per week and all-cause mortality and cardiovascular disease mortality in middle-aged and elderly men. The greatest potential for reduced mortality is seen in sedentary individuals who become moderately active. Studies have shown that since heart disease is the leading cause of death in women, regular exercise in aging women leads to healthier cardiovascular profiles. Most beneficial effects of physical activity on cardiovascular disease mortality can be attained through moderate-intensity activity (40–60% of maximal oxygen uptake, depending on age). Persons who modify their behavior after myocardial infarction to include regular exercise have improved rates of survival. Persons who remain sedentary have the highest risk for all-cause and cardiovascular disease mortality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/American_Heart_Association" title="American Heart Association">American Heart Association</a>, exercise reduces the risk of cardiovascular diseases, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heart_attack" title="Heart attack">heart attack</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stroke" title="Stroke">stroke</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aha2017_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-aha2017-26">[26]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some have suggested that increases in physical exercise might decrease healthcare costs, increase the rate of job attendance, as well as increase the amount of effort women put into their jobs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Immune_system">Immune system</span></h3>
<p>Although there have been hundreds of studies on physical exercise and the <a href="/wiki/Immune_system" title="Immune system">immune system</a>, there is little direct evidence on its connection to illness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gleeson2007_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gleeson2007-31">[31]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Epidemiology" title="Epidemiology">Epidemiological</a> evidence suggests that moderate exercise has a beneficial effect on the human <a href="/wiki/Immune_system" title="Immune system">immune system</a>; an effect which is modeled in a <a href="/wiki/J_curve" title="J curve">J curve</a>. Moderate exercise has been associated with a 29% decreased incidence of <a href="/wiki/Upper_respiratory_tract_infection" title="Upper respiratory tract infection">upper respiratory tract infections</a> (URTI), but studies of marathon runners found that their prolonged high-intensity exercise was associated with an increased risk of infection occurrence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gleeson2007_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gleeson2007-31">[31]</a></sup> However, another study did not find the effect. Immune cell functions are impaired following acute sessions of prolonged, high-intensity exercise, and some studies have found that athletes are at a higher risk for infections. Studies have shown that strenuous stress for long durations, such as training for a marathon, can suppress the immune system by decreasing the concentration of lymphocytes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> The immune systems of athletes and nonathletes are generally similar. Athletes may have a slightly elevated <a href="/wiki/Natural_killer_cell" title="Natural killer cell">natural killer cell</a> count and cytolytic action, but these are unlikely to be clinically significant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gleeson2007_31-2"><a href="#cite_note-Gleeson2007-31">[31]</a></sup>
</p><p>Vitamin C supplementation has been associated with a lower incidence of <a href="/wiki/Upper_respiratory_tract_infection" title="Upper respiratory tract infection">upper respiratory tract infections</a> in marathon runners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gleeson2007_31-3"><a href="#cite_note-Gleeson2007-31">[31]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Biomarker" title="Biomarker">Biomarkers</a> of <a href="/wiki/Inflammation" title="Inflammation">inflammation</a> such as <a href="/wiki/C-reactive_protein" title="C-reactive protein">C-reactive protein</a>, which are associated with chronic diseases, are reduced in active individuals relative to sedentary individuals, and the positive effects of exercise may be due to its anti-inflammatory effects. In individuals with heart disease, exercise interventions lower blood levels of fibrinogen and C-reactive protein, an important cardiovascular risk marker.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Swardfager2012_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Swardfager2012-33">[33]</a></sup> The depression in the immune system following acute bouts of exercise may be one of the mechanisms for this anti-inflammatory effect.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gleeson2007_31-4"><a href="#cite_note-Gleeson2007-31">[31]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cancer">Cancer</span></h3>
<p>A systematic review evaluated 45 studies that examined the relationship between physical activity and cancer survival rates. According to the review, "[there] was consistent evidence from 27 observational studies that physical activity is associated with reduced all-cause, breast cancer–specific, and colon cancer–specific mortality. There is currently insufficient evidence regarding the association between physical activity and mortality for survivors of other cancers."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Evidence suggests that exercise may positively affect the quality of life in cancer survivors, including factors such as anxiety, self-esteem and emotional well-being.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> For people with cancer undergoing active treatment, exercise may also have positive effects on health-related quality of life, such as fatigue and physical functioning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-36">[36]</a></sup> This is likely to be more pronounced with higher intensity exercise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-36">[36]</a></sup>
</p><p>Exercise may contribute to a reduction of <a href="/wiki/Cancer-related_fatigue" title="Cancer-related fatigue">cancer-related fatigue</a> in survivors of <a href="/wiki/Breast_cancer" title="Breast cancer">breast cancer</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Although there is only limited scientific evidence on the subject, people with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cancer_cachexia" title="Cancer cachexia">cancer cachexia</a> are encouraged to engage in physical exercise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid26401466_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid26401466-38">[38]</a></sup> Due to various factors, some individuals with cancer cachexia have a limited capacity for physical exercise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid29891116_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid29891116-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid29440149_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid29440149-40">[40]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Compliance_(medicine)" title="Compliance (medicine)">Compliance</a> with prescribed exercise is low in individuals with cachexia and clinical trials of exercise in this population often have high drop-out rates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid29891116_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-pmid29891116-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid29440149_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-pmid29440149-40">[40]</a></sup>
</p><p>There is low-quality evidence for an effect of aerobic physical exercises on anxiety and serious adverse events in adults with <a href="/wiki/Tumors_of_the_hematopoietic_and_lymphoid_tissues" title="Tumors of the hematopoietic and lymphoid tissues">hematological malignancies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-:3-41">[41]</a></sup> Aerobic physical exercise may result in little to no difference in the mortality, quality of life, or physical functioning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-:3-41">[41]</a></sup> These exercises may result in a slight reduction in depression and reduction in fatigue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_41-2"><a href="#cite_note-:3-41">[41]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Neurobiological">Neurobiological<span class="anchor" id="Brain_function"></span></span></h3>
<div class="excerpt-block"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066933788">.mw-parser-output .excerpt-hat .mw-editsection-like{font-style:normal}</style><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise" title="Neurobiological effects of physical exercise">Neurobiological effects of physical exercise</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise" title="Neurobiological effects of physical exercise">neurobiological effects of physical exercise</a> are numerous and involve a wide range of interrelated effects on brain structure, brain function, and <a href="/wiki/Cognition" title="Cognition">cognition</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Summary_as_of_August_2015_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Summary_as_of_August_2015-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_–_neurotrophic_factors_+_basal_ganglia_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_–_neurotrophic_factors_+_basal_ganglia-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Summary_of_effects_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Summary_of_effects-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_epigenome_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_epigenome-45">[45]</a></sup> A large body of research in humans has demonstrated that consistent <a href="/wiki/Aerobic_exercise" title="Aerobic exercise">aerobic exercise</a> (e.g., 30 minutes every day) induces persistent improvements in certain <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cognitive_function" title="Cognitive function">cognitive functions</a>, healthy alterations in <a href="/wiki/Gene_expression" title="Gene expression">gene expression</a> in the brain, and beneficial forms of <a href="/wiki/Neuroplasticity" title="Neuroplasticity">neuroplasticity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Behavioral_plasticity" title="Behavioral plasticity">behavioral plasticity</a>; some of these long-term effects include: increased <a href="/wiki/Adult_neurogenesis" title="Adult neurogenesis">neuron growth</a>, increased neurological activity (e.g., <span class="nowrap"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C-Fos" title="C-Fos">c-Fos</a></span> and <a href="/wiki/Brain-derived_neurotrophic_factor" title="Brain-derived neurotrophic factor">BDNF</a> signaling), improved stress coping, enhanced <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cognitive_control_of_behavior" title="Cognitive control of behavior">cognitive control of behavior</a>, improved <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Declarative_memory" title="Declarative memory">declarative</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spatial_memory" title="Spatial memory">spatial</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Working_memory" title="Working memory">working</a> memory, and structural and functional improvements in brain structures and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neural_pathways" title="Neural pathways">pathways</a> associated with cognitive control and memory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Summary_as_of_August_2015_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Summary_as_of_August_2015-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_–_neurotrophic_factors_+_basal_ganglia_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_–_neurotrophic_factors_+_basal_ganglia-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Summary_of_effects_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Summary_of_effects-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_epigenome_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_epigenome-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Comprehensive_review_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Comprehensive_review-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_gray_matter_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_gray_matter-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_exercise_benefits_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_exercise_benefits-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_BDNF_depression_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_BDNF_depression-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_cognitive_control_of_exercise_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_cognitive_control_of_exercise-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_healthy_young_adult_2016_SystRev_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_healthy_young_adult_2016_SystRev-51">[51]</a></sup> The effects of exercise on cognition have important implications for improving <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academic_performance" title="Academic performance">academic performance</a> in children and college students, improving adult productivity, preserving <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cognitive_function" title="Cognitive function">cognitive function</a> in old age, preventing or treating certain <a href="/wiki/Neurological_disorder" title="Neurological disorder">neurological disorders</a>, and improving overall <a href="/wiki/Quality_of_life" title="Quality of life">quality of life</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Summary_as_of_August_2015_42-2"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Summary_as_of_August_2015-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Depression_QoL_meta-analysis_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Depression_QoL_meta-analysis-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Aging_QoL_review_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Aging_QoL_review-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup>
</p><p>In healthy adults, aerobic exercise has been shown to induce transient effects on cognition after a single exercise session and persistent effects on cognition following regular exercise over the course of several months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Summary_as_of_August_2015_42-3"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Summary_as_of_August_2015-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_healthy_young_adult_2016_SystRev_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_healthy_young_adult_2016_SystRev-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Neurobiological_effects_of_acute_exercise_–_2017_review_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Neurobiological_effects_of_acute_exercise_–_2017_review-55">[55]</a></sup> People who regularly perform aerobic exercise (e.g., running, <a href="/wiki/Jogging" title="Jogging">jogging</a>, brisk walking, swimming, and cycling) have greater scores on <a href="/wiki/Neuropsychological_test" title="Neuropsychological test">neuropsychological function and performance tests</a> that measure certain cognitive functions, such as <a href="/wiki/Attentional_control" title="Attentional control">attentional control</a>, <a href="/wiki/Inhibitory_control" title="Inhibitory control">inhibitory control</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cognitive_flexibility" title="Cognitive flexibility">cognitive flexibility</a>, <a href="/wiki/Working_memory" title="Working memory">working memory</a> updating and capacity, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Declarative_memory" title="Declarative memory">declarative memory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spatial_memory" title="Spatial memory">spatial memory</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mental_chronometry" title="Mental chronometry">information processing speed</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Summary_as_of_August_2015_42-4"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Summary_as_of_August_2015-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Comprehensive_review_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Comprehensive_review-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_exercise_benefits_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_exercise_benefits-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_cognitive_control_of_exercise_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_cognitive_control_of_exercise-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_healthy_young_adult_2016_SystRev_51-2"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_healthy_young_adult_2016_SystRev-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Neurobiological_effects_of_acute_exercise_–_2017_review_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Neurobiological_effects_of_acute_exercise_–_2017_review-55">[55]</a></sup> The transient effects of exercise on cognition include improvements in most executive functions (e.g., attention, working memory, cognitive flexibility, inhibitory control, problem solving, and decision making) and information processing speed for a period of up to 2 hours after exercising.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Neurobiological_effects_of_acute_exercise_–_2017_review_55-2"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Neurobiological_effects_of_acute_exercise_–_2017_review-55">[55]</a></sup>
</p><p>Aerobic exercise induces short- and long-term effects on mood and emotional states by promoting <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Positive_affect" title="Positive affect">positive affect</a>, inhibiting <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Negative_affect" title="Negative affect">negative affect</a>, and decreasing the biological response to acute <a href="/wiki/Psychological_stress" title="Psychological stress">psychological stress</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Neurobiological_effects_of_acute_exercise_–_2017_review_55-3"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Neurobiological_effects_of_acute_exercise_–_2017_review-55">[55]</a></sup> Over the short-term, aerobic exercise functions as both an <a href="/wiki/Antidepressant" title="Antidepressant">antidepressant</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euphoriant" title="Euphoriant">euphoriant</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Euphoria_review_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Euphoria_review-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Runner_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Runner-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_depression_intervention_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_depression_intervention-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Physical_activity_intervention_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Physical_activity_intervention-59">[59]</a></sup> whereas consistent exercise produces general improvements in <a href="/wiki/Mood_(psychology)" title="Mood (psychology)">mood</a> and <a href="/wiki/Self-esteem" title="Self-esteem">self-esteem</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_BDNF_meta_analysis_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_BDNF_meta_analysis-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_children_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_children-61">[61]</a></sup>
</p>
Regular aerobic exercise improves symptoms associated with a variety of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_nervous_system_disorders" title="Central nervous system disorders">central nervous system disorders</a> and may be used as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adjunct_therapy" title="Adjunct therapy">adjunct therapy</a> for these disorders.  There is clear evidence of exercise treatment efficacy for <a href="/wiki/Major_depressive_disorder" title="Major depressive disorder">major depressive disorder</a> and <a href="/wiki/Attention_deficit_hyperactivity_disorder" title="Attention deficit hyperactivity disorder">attention deficit hyperactivity disorder</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Depression_QoL_meta-analysis_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Depression_QoL_meta-analysis-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_depression_intervention_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_depression_intervention-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_MDD_antidepressant_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_MDD_antidepressant-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_ADHD_exercise_2016_SystRev_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_ADHD_exercise_2016_SystRev-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_ADHD_Exercise_2014_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_ADHD_Exercise_2014-64">[64]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Neurology" title="American Academy of Neurology">American Academy of Neurology</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clinical_practice_guideline" title="Clinical practice guideline">clinical practice guideline</a> for <a href="/wiki/Mild_cognitive_impairment" title="Mild cognitive impairment">mild cognitive impairment</a> indicates that clinicians should recommend regular exercise (two times per week) to individuals who have been diagnosed with this condition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_December_2017_AAN_Clinical_Practice_Guideline_for_MCI_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_December_2017_AAN_Clinical_Practice_Guideline_for_MCI-65">[65]</a></sup> Reviews of clinical evidence also support the use of exercise as an adjunct therapy for certain <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neurodegenerative_disorder" title="Neurodegenerative disorder">neurodegenerative disorders</a>, particularly <a href="/wiki/Alzheimer%27s_disease" title="Alzheimer's disease">Alzheimer's disease</a> and <a href="/wiki/Parkinson%27s_disease" title="Parkinson's disease">Parkinson's disease</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Alz_1_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Alz_1-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Alz_2_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Alz_2-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Parkinson_1_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Parkinson_1-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Parkinson_2_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Parkinson_2-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Parkinson_3_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Parkinson_3-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Parkinson_physiotherapy_Cochrane_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Parkinson_physiotherapy_Cochrane-71">[71]</a></sup> Regular exercise is also associated with a lower risk of developing neurodegenerative disorders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Parkinson_2_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Parkinson_2-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Longitudinal_SystRev_dementia_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Longitudinal_SystRev_dementia-72">[72]</a></sup> A large body of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Preclinical" title="Preclinical">preclinical</a> evidence and emerging clinical evidence supports the use of exercise as an adjunct therapy for the treatment and prevention of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drug_addiction" title="Drug addiction">drug addictions</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Addiction_review_2016_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Addiction_review_2016-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Running_vs_addiction_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Running_vs_addiction-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Natural_and_drug_addictions_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Natural_and_drug_addictions-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_Rev_3_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_Rev_3-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise,_addiction_prevention,_and_ΔFosB_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise,_addiction_prevention,_and_ΔFosB-77">[77]</a></sup> Regular exercise has also been proposed as an adjunct therapy for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brain_cancer" title="Brain cancer">brain cancers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Neurooncology_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Neurooncology-78">[78]</a></sup></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Depression">Depression</span></h4>
<blockquote class="excerpt-block"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066933788" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise#Major_depressive_disorder" title="Neurobiological effects of physical exercise">Neurobiological effects of physical exercise § Major depressive disorder</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<p>A number of medical reviews have indicated that exercise has a marked and persistent <a href="/wiki/Antidepressant" title="Antidepressant">antidepressant</a> effect in humans,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Comprehensive_review_46-2"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Comprehensive_review-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_depression_intervention_58-2"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_depression_intervention-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Physical_activity_intervention_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Physical_activity_intervention-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_MDD_antidepressant_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_MDD_antidepressant-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Cochrane_exercise_depression_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Cochrane_exercise_depression-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Running_antidepressant_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Running_antidepressant-80">[80]</a></sup> an effect believed to be mediated through enhanced <abbr title="brain-derived neurotrophic factor">BDNF</abbr> signaling in the brain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_BDNF_depression_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_BDNF_depression-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_MDD_antidepressant_62-2"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_MDD_antidepressant-62">[62]</a></sup> Several systematic reviews have analyzed the potential for physical exercise in the treatment of <a href="/wiki/Major_depressive_disorder" title="Major depressive disorder">depressive disorders</a>. The 2013 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cochrane_Collaboration" title="Cochrane Collaboration">Cochrane Collaboration</a> review on physical exercise for depression noted that, based upon limited evidence, it is more effective than a control intervention and comparable to psychological or antidepressant drug therapies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Cochrane_exercise_depression_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Cochrane_exercise_depression-79">[79]</a></sup> Three subsequent 2014 systematic reviews that included the Cochrane review in their analysis concluded with similar findings: one indicated that physical exercise is effective as an <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/adjunct_treatment" title="wikt:adjunct treatment">adjunct treatment</a> (i.e., treatments that are used together) with antidepressant medication;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_MDD_antidepressant_62-3"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_MDD_antidepressant-62">[62]</a></sup> the other two indicated that physical exercise has marked antidepressant effects and recommended the inclusion of physical activity as an adjunct treatment for mild–moderate depression and mental illness in general.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_depression_intervention_58-3"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_depression_intervention-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Physical_activity_intervention_59-2"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Physical_activity_intervention-59">[59]</a></sup> One systematic review noted that <a href="/wiki/Modern_yoga" title="Modern yoga">yoga</a> may be effective in alleviating symptoms of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prenatal_depression" title="Prenatal depression">prenatal depression</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Yoga_depression_SystRev_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Yoga_depression_SystRev-81">[81]</a></sup> Another review asserted that evidence from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clinical_trials" title="Clinical trials">clinical trials</a> supports the efficacy of physical exercise as a treatment for depression over a 2–4 month period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Comprehensive_review_46-3"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Comprehensive_review-46">[46]</a></sup> These benefits have also been noted in <a href="/wiki/Old_age" title="Old age">old age</a>, with a review conducted in 2019 finding that exercise is an effective treatment for clinically diagnosed depression in older adults.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_miller2020_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_miller2020-82">[82]</a></sup>
</p>
A <a href="/wiki/Meta-analysis" title="Meta-analysis">meta-analysis</a> from July 2016 concluded that physical exercise improves overall quality of life in individuals with depression relative to controls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Depression_QoL_meta-analysis_52-2"><a href="#cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Depression_QoL_meta-analysis-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></div></blockquote>
<p>Continuous aerobic exercise can induce a transient state of <a href="/wiki/Euphoria" title="Euphoria">euphoria</a>, colloquially known as a "runner's high" in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Distance_running" title="Distance running">distance running</a> or a "rower's high" in <a href="/wiki/Rowing_(sport)" title="Rowing (sport)">crew</a>, through the increased biosynthesis of at least three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euphoriant" title="Euphoriant">euphoriant</a> neurochemicals: <a href="/wiki/Anandamide" title="Anandamide">anandamide</a> (an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endocannabinoid" title="Endocannabinoid">endocannabinoid</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-endocannabinoids_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-endocannabinoids-84">[84]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%CE%92-endorphin" title="Β-endorphin">β-endorphin</a> (an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endogenous_opioid" title="Endogenous opioid">endogenous opioid</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Endorphin_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Endorphin-85">[85]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Phenethylamine" title="Phenethylamine">phenethylamine</a> (a <a href="/wiki/Trace_amine" title="Trace amine">trace amine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amphetamine" title="Amphetamine">amphetamine</a> analog).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PEA_exercise_primary_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-PEA_exercise_primary-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Renaissance_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Renaissance-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neuropsychiatric_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neuropsychiatric-88">[88]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sleep">Sleep</span></h3>
<p>Preliminary evidence from a 2012 review indicated that physical training for up to four months may increase sleep quality in adults over 40 years of age.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> A 2010 review suggested that exercise generally improved <a href="/wiki/Sleep" title="Sleep">sleep</a> for most people, and may help with <a href="/wiki/Insomnia" title="Insomnia">insomnia</a>, but there is insufficient evidence to draw detailed conclusions about the relationship between exercise and sleep.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> A 2018 systematic review and meta-analysis suggested that exercise can improve sleep quality in people with insomnia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libido">Libido</span></h3>
<p>One 2013 study found that exercising improved sexual arousal problems related to antidepressant use.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Respiratory_system">Respiratory system</span></h3>
<p>People who participate in physical exercise experience increased cardiovascular fitness.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources_(medicine)" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources (medicine)"><span title="Material near this tag needs references to reliable medical sources. (May 2022)">medical citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
There is some level of concern about additional exposure to air pollution when <a href="/wiki/Outdoor_fitness" title="Outdoor fitness">exercising outdoors</a>, especially near traffic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Laeremans_et_al._2018_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-Laeremans_et_al._2018-93">[93]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mechanism_of_effects">Mechanism of effects</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Skeletal_muscle">Skeletal muscle</span></h3>
<p>Resistance training and subsequent consumption of a protein-rich meal promotes <a href="/wiki/Muscle_hypertrophy" title="Muscle hypertrophy">muscle hypertrophy</a> and gains in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muscle_strength" title="Muscle strength">muscle strength</a> by stimulating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Myofibrillar" title="Myofibrillar">myofibrillar</a> muscle protein synthesis (MPS) and inhibiting muscle protein breakdown (MPB).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Skeletal_muscle_homeostasis_2016_review_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-Skeletal_muscle_homeostasis_2016_review-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Muscle_hypertrophy_review_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-Muscle_hypertrophy_review-95">[95]</a></sup> The stimulation of muscle protein synthesis by resistance training occurs via <a href="/wiki/Phosphorylation" title="Phosphorylation">phosphorylation</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mechanistic_target_of_rapamycin" title="Mechanistic target of rapamycin">mechanistic target of rapamycin</a> (mTOR) and subsequent activation of <a href="/wiki/MTORC1" title="MTORC1">mTORC1</a>, which leads to <a href="/wiki/Protein_biosynthesis" title="Protein biosynthesis">protein biosynthesis</a> in cellular <a href="/wiki/Ribosome" title="Ribosome">ribosomes</a> via phosphorylation of mTORC1's immediate targets (the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/P70S6_kinase" title="P70S6 kinase">p70S6 kinase</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protein_translation" title="Protein translation">translation</a> repressor protein <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/4EBP1" title="4EBP1">4EBP1</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Skeletal_muscle_homeostasis_2016_review_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-Skeletal_muscle_homeostasis_2016_review-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Molecular_Aspects_of_Medicine_2016_review_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-Molecular_Aspects_of_Medicine_2016_review-96">[96]</a></sup> The suppression of muscle protein breakdown following food consumption occurs primarily via increases in <a href="/wiki/Blood_plasma" title="Blood plasma">plasma</a> <a href="/wiki/Insulin" title="Insulin">insulin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Skeletal_muscle_homeostasis_2016_review_94-2"><a href="#cite_note-Skeletal_muscle_homeostasis_2016_review-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HMB_in_vivo_human_pharmacodynamics_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-HMB_in_vivo_human_pharmacodynamics-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pharmacodynamics_and_pharmacokinetics_of_HMB-CA_in_humans_in_vivo_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pharmacodynamics_and_pharmacokinetics_of_HMB-CA_in_humans_in_vivo-98">[98]</a></sup> Similarly, increased muscle protein synthesis (via activation of mTORC1) and suppressed muscle protein breakdown (via insulin-independent mechanisms) has also been shown to occur following ingestion of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%CE%92-hydroxy_%CE%B2-methylbutyric_acid" title="Β-hydroxy β-methylbutyric acid">β-hydroxy β-methylbutyric acid</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Skeletal_muscle_homeostasis_2016_review_94-3"><a href="#cite_note-Skeletal_muscle_homeostasis_2016_review-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HMB_in_vivo_human_pharmacodynamics_97-1"><a href="#cite_note-HMB_in_vivo_human_pharmacodynamics-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pharmacodynamics_and_pharmacokinetics_of_HMB-CA_in_humans_in_vivo_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-Pharmacodynamics_and_pharmacokinetics_of_HMB-CA_in_humans_in_vivo-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sarcopenia_July_2015_review_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sarcopenia_July_2015_review-99">[99]</a></sup>
</p><p>Aerobic exercise induces <a href="/wiki/Mitochondrial_biogenesis" title="Mitochondrial biogenesis">mitochondrial biogenesis</a> and an increased capacity for <a href="/wiki/Oxidative_phosphorylation" title="Oxidative phosphorylation">oxidative phosphorylation</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mitochondria" title="Mitochondria">mitochondria</a> of skeletal muscle, which is one mechanism by which aerobic exercise enhances submaximal endurance performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Skeletal_muscle_homeostasis_2016_review_94-4"><a href="#cite_note-Skeletal_muscle_homeostasis_2016_review-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aerobic_exercise_–_mitochondrial_biogenesis_and_OXPHOS_capacity_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Aerobic_exercise_–_mitochondrial_biogenesis_and_OXPHOS_capacity-101">[101]</a></sup> These effects occur via an exercise-induced increase in the intracellular <a href="/wiki/Adenosine_monophosphate" title="Adenosine monophosphate">AMP</a>:<a href="/wiki/Adenosine_triphosphate" title="Adenosine triphosphate">ATP</a> ratio, thereby triggering the activation of <a href="/wiki/AMP-activated_protein_kinase" title="AMP-activated protein kinase">AMP-activated protein kinase</a> (AMPK) which subsequently phosphorylates <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PGC-1%CE%B1" title="PGC-1α">peroxisome proliferator-activated receptor gamma coactivator-1α</a> (PGC-1α), the <a href="/wiki/Master_regulator" title="Master regulator">master regulator</a> of mitochondrial biogenesis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Skeletal_muscle_homeostasis_2016_review_94-5"><a href="#cite_note-Skeletal_muscle_homeostasis_2016_review-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aerobic_exercise_–_mitochondrial_biogenesis_and_OXPHOS_capacity_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-Aerobic_exercise_–_mitochondrial_biogenesis_and_OXPHOS_capacity-101">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mitochondrial_biogenesis_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mitochondrial_biogenesis-102">[102]</a></sup>
</p>

title="Amino acid">amino acids</a> or their derivatives (primarily <a href="/wiki/Leucine" title="Leucine"><span class="nowrap"><span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">L</span></span>-leucine</span></a> and <a href="/wiki/Beta-Hydroxy_beta-methylbutyric_acid" title="Beta-Hydroxy beta-methylbutyric acid">HMB</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Skeletal_muscle_homeostasis_2016_review_94-6"><a href="#cite_note-Skeletal_muscle_homeostasis_2016_review-94">[94]</a></sup> Many amino acids derived from food protein promote the activation of <a href="/wiki/MTORC1" title="MTORC1">mTORC1</a> and increase <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protein_translation" title="Protein translation">protein synthesis</a> by <a href="/wiki/Signal_transduction" title="Signal transduction">signaling</a> through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rag_GTPase" title="Rag GTPase">Rag GTPases</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Skeletal_muscle_homeostasis_2016_review_94-7"><a href="#cite_note-Skeletal_muscle_homeostasis_2016_review-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_peripheral_organs">Other peripheral organs</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aerobic_Anaerobic_Exercise_Adaptations.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="431" data-file-width="579" decoding="async" height="298" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Aerobic_Anaerobic_Exercise_Adaptations.jpg/400px-Aerobic_Anaerobic_Exercise_Adaptations.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f6/Aerobic_Anaerobic_Exercise_Adaptations.jpg 1.5x" width="400"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aerobic_Anaerobic_Exercise_Adaptations.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Summary of long-term adaptations to regular aerobic and anaerobic exercise. Aerobic exercise can cause several central cardiovascular adaptations, including an increase in <a href="/wiki/Stroke_volume" title="Stroke volume">stroke volume</a> (SV)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Exercise_SV_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-Exercise_SV-104">[104]</a></sup> and maximal aerobic capacity (<a href="/wiki/VO2_max" title="VO2 max">VO<sub>2</sub> max</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Exercise_SV_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-Exercise_SV-104">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AerobicMotorCapability_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-AerobicMotorCapability-105">[105]</a></sup> as well as a decrease in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Resting_heart_rate" title="Resting heart rate">resting heart rate</a> (RHR).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Exercise_RHR1_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-Exercise_RHR1-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Exercise_RHR2_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-Exercise_RHR2-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Exercise_RHR3_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-Exercise_RHR3-108">[108]</a></sup> Long-term adaptations to resistance training, the most common form of anaerobic exercise, include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muscular_hypertrophy" title="Muscular hypertrophy">muscular hypertrophy</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Exercise_Hypertrophy_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-Exercise_Hypertrophy-109">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Exercise_Hypertrophy2_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-Exercise_Hypertrophy2-110">[110]</a></sup> an increase in the <a href="/wiki/Physiological_cross-sectional_area" title="Physiological cross-sectional area">physiological cross-sectional area</a> (PCSA) of muscle(s), and an increase in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neural_drive" title="Neural drive">neural drive</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Exercise_Neuraldrive_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-Exercise_Neuraldrive-111">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AnaerobicStrength_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-AnaerobicStrength-112">[112]</a></sup> both of which lead to increased <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muscular_strength" title="Muscular strength">muscular strength</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Exercise_MuscularStrength_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-Exercise_MuscularStrength-113">[113]</a></sup> Neural adaptations begin more quickly and plateau prior to the hypertrophic response.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NeuralvsHypertrophy1_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-NeuralvsHypertrophy1-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NeuralvsHypertrophy2_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-NeuralvsHypertrophy2-115">[115]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Developing research has demonstrated that many of the benefits of exercise are mediated through the role of skeletal muscle as an endocrine organ. That is, contracting muscles release multiple substances known as <a href="/wiki/Myokine" title="Myokine">myokines</a> which promote the growth of new tissue, tissue repair, and multiple anti-inflammatory functions, which in turn reduce the risk of developing various inflammatory diseases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> Exercise reduces levels of <a href="/wiki/Cortisol" title="Cortisol">cortisol</a>, which causes many health problems, both physical and mental.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> Endurance exercise before meals lowers <a href="/wiki/Blood_sugar_level" title="Blood sugar level">blood glucose</a> more than the same exercise after meals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> There is evidence that vigorous exercise (90–95% of <a href="/wiki/VO2_max" title="VO2 max">VO<sub>2</sub> max</a>) induces a greater degree of physiological <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardiac_hypertrophy" title="Cardiac hypertrophy">cardiac hypertrophy</a> than moderate exercise (40 to 70% of VO<sub>2</sub> max), but it is unknown whether this has any effects on overall morbidity and/or mortality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> Both aerobic and anaerobic exercise work to increase the mechanical efficiency of the heart by increasing cardiac volume (aerobic exercise), or myocardial thickness (strength training). <a href="/wiki/Ventricular_hypertrophy" title="Ventricular hypertrophy">Ventricular hypertrophy</a>, the thickening of the ventricular walls, is generally beneficial and healthy if it occurs in response to exercise.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Central_nervous_system">Central nervous system</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise#Neuroplasticity" title="Neurobiological effects of physical exercise">Neurobiological effects of physical exercise § Neuroplasticity</a></div>
<p>The effects of physical exercise on the <a href="/wiki/Central_nervous_system" title="Central nervous system">central nervous system</a> are mediated in part by specific <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neurotrophic_factor" title="Neurotrophic factor">neurotrophic factor</a> <a href="/wiki/Myokine" title="Myokine">hormones that are released into the blood stream by muscles</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Brain-derived_neurotrophic_factor" title="Brain-derived neurotrophic factor">BDNF</a>, <a href="/wiki/Insulin-like_growth_factor_1" title="Insulin-like growth factor 1">IGF-1</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vascular_endothelial_growth_factor" title="Vascular endothelial growth factor">VEGF</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Exercise_–_neurotrophic_factors_+_basal_ganglia_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-Exercise_–_neurotrophic_factors_+_basal_ganglia-120">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BDNF_meta_analysis_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-BDNF_meta_analysis-121">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VEGF_aging_brain_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-VEGF_aging_brain-122">[122]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fitness_mechanism_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fitness_mechanism-123">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Comprehensive_review_–_repeat_citation_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-Comprehensive_review_–_repeat_citation-124">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cerebral_hemodynamics_and_AD_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cerebral_hemodynamics_and_AD-125">[125]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_health_measures">Public health measures</span></h2>
<p>Community-wide and school campaigns are often used in an attempt to increase a population's level of physical activity. Studies to determine the effectiveness of these types of programs need to be interpreted cautiously as the results vary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-17">[17]</a></sup> There is some evidence that certain types of exercise programmes for older adults, such as those involving gait, balance, co-ordination and functional tasks, can improve balance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> Following progressive resistance training, older adults also respond with improved physical function.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> Brief interventions promoting physical activity may be cost-effective, however this evidence is weak and there are variations between studies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup>
</p><p>Environmental approaches appear promising: signs that encourage the use of stairs, as well as community campaigns, may increase exercise levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> The city of <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1" title="Bogotá">Bogotá</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, for example, blocks off 113 kilometers (70 mi) of roads on Sundays and holidays to make it easier for its citizens to get exercise. Such <a href="/wiki/Pedestrian_zone" title="Pedestrian zone">pedestrian zones</a> are part of an effort to combat chronic diseases and to maintain a healthy <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Body_Mass_Index" title="Body Mass Index">BMI</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dons_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dons-131">[131]</a></sup>
</p><p>Parents can promote physical activity by modelling healthy levels of physical activity or by encouraging physical activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> According to the Centers for Disease Control and Prevention in the United States, children and adolescents should do 60 minutes or more of physical activity each day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> Implementing physical exercise in the school system and ensuring an environment in which children can reduce barriers to maintain a healthy lifestyle is essential.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>'s Directorate-General for Education and Culture (DG EAC) has dedicated programs and funds for Health Enhancing Physical Activity (HEPA) projects<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> within its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Horizon_2020" title="Horizon 2020">Horizon 2020</a> and <a href="/wiki/Erasmus%2B" title="Erasmus+">Erasmus+</a> program, as research showed that too many Europeans are not physically active enough. Financing is available for increased collaboration between players active in this field across the EU and around the world, the promotion of HEPA in the EU and its partner countries, and the European Sports Week. The DG EAC regularly publishes a <a href="/wiki/Eurobarometer" title="Eurobarometer">Eurobarometer</a> on sport and physical activity.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Exercise_trends">Exercise trends</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Exercise_trends" title="Exercise trends">Exercise trends</a></div>
<p>Worldwide there has been a large shift toward less physically demanding work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2009_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2009-135">[135]</a></sup> This has been accompanied by increasing use of mechanized transportation, a greater prevalence of labor-saving technology in the home, and fewer active <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Recreational_pursuits" title="Recreational pursuits">recreational pursuits</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2009_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2009-135">[135]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Exercise_trends#Solutions_to_address_the_lack_of_exercise" title="Exercise trends">Personal lifestyle changes</a>, however, can correct the lack of physical exercise.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources_(medicine)" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources (medicine)"><span title="Material near this tag needs references to reliable medical sources. (May 2022)">medical citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Research published in 2015 suggests that incorporating <a href="/wiki/Mindfulness" title="Mindfulness">mindfulness</a> into physical exercise interventions increases exercise adherence and self-efficacy, and also has positive effects both psychologically and physiologically.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kennedy_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kennedy-136">[136]</a></sup>
</p>
