</div></li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 185px"><div style="width: 185px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 180px;"><div style="margin:24.5px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cristiano_Ronaldo_Iran_vs_Portugal.jpg" title="Football as an exercise"><img alt="Football as an exercise" data-file-height="853" data-file-width="980" decoding="async" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Cristiano_Ronaldo_Iran_vs_Portugal.jpg/150px-Cristiano_Ronaldo_Iran_vs_Portugal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Cristiano_Ronaldo_Iran_vs_Portugal.jpg/225px-Cristiano_Ronaldo_Iran_vs_Portugal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Cristiano_Ronaldo_Iran_vs_Portugal.jpg/300px-Cristiano_Ronaldo_Iran_vs_Portugal.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> as an exercise
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_and_cultural_variation">Social and cultural variation</span></h3>
<p>Exercising looks different in every country, as do the motivations behind exercising.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fitness_for_Foreigners_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fitness_for_Foreigners-3">[3]</a></sup> In some countries, people exercise primarily indoors (such as at home or <a href="/wiki/Health_club" title="Health club">health clubs</a>), while in others, people primarily <a href="/wiki/Outdoor_fitness" title="Outdoor fitness">exercise outdoors</a>. People may exercise for personal enjoyment, health and well-being, social interactions, competition or training, etc. These differences could potentially be attributed to a variety of reasons including geographic location and social tendencies.
</p><p>In Colombia, for example, citizens value and celebrate the outdoor environments of their country. In many instances, they utilize outdoor activities as social gatherings to enjoy nature and their communities. In Bogotá, Colombia, a 70-mile stretch of road known as the Ciclovía is shut down each Sunday for bicyclists, runners, rollerbladers, skateboarders and other exercisers to work out and enjoy their surroundings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup>
</p><p>Similarly to Colombia, citizens of <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a> tend to exercise socially outside. In this country, public gyms have become quite popular. People will congregate at these outdoor gyms not only to utilize the public facilities, but also to organize aerobics and dance sessions, which are open to the public.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup>
</p><p>Sweden has also begun developing outdoor gyms, called <i>utegym</i>. These gyms are free to the public and are often placed in beautiful, picturesque environments. People will swim in rivers, use boats, and run through forests to stay healthy and enjoy the natural world around them. This works particularly well in Sweden due to its geographical location.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup>
</p><p>Exercise in some areas of China, particularly among those who are retired, seems to be socially grounded. In the mornings, <a href="/wiki/Square_dancing_(China)" title="Square dancing (China)">square dances</a> are held in public parks; these gatherings may include Latin dancing, ballroom dancing, tango, or even the jitterbug. Dancing in public allows people to interact with those with whom they would not normally interact, allowing for both health and social benefits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup>
</p><p>These sociocultural variations in physical exercise show how people in different geographic locations and social climates have varying motivations and methods of exercising. Physical exercise can improve health and well-being, as well as enhance community ties and appreciation of natural beauty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fitness_for_Foreigners_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-Fitness_for_Foreigners-3">[3]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Nutrition_and_recovery">Nutrition and recovery</span></h2>
<p>Proper <a href="/wiki/Nutrition" title="Nutrition">nutrition</a> is as important to health as exercise. When exercising, it becomes even more important to have a good diet to ensure that the body has the correct ratio of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macronutrient_(nutrition)" title="Macronutrient (nutrition)">macronutrients</a> while providing ample <a href="/wiki/Micronutrient" title="Micronutrient">micronutrients</a>, in order to aid the body with the recovery process following strenuous exercise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup>
</p><p>Active recovery is recommended after participating in physical exercise because it removes <a href="/wiki/Lactic_acid" title="Lactic acid">lactate</a> from the blood more quickly than inactive recovery. Removing lactate from circulation allows for an easy decline in body temperature, which can also benefit the immune system, as an individual may be vulnerable to minor illnesses if the body temperature drops too abruptly after physical exercise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid16195010_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid16195010-145">[145]</a></sup>
</p><p>Exercise has an effect on appetite, but whether it increases or decreases appetite varies from individual to individual, and is affected by the intensity and duration of the exercise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Excessive_exercise">Excessive exercise</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Overtraining" title="Overtraining">Overtraining</a></div>
<p>Excessive exercise or <a href="/wiki/Overtraining" title="Overtraining">overtraining</a> occurs when a person exceeds their body's ability to recover from strenuous exercise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097763485">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+link+.ambox{margin-top:-1px}html body.mediawiki .mw-parser-output .ambox.mbox-small-left{margin:4px 1em 4px 0;overflow:hidden;width:238px;border-collapse:collapse;font-size:88%;line-height:1.25em}.mw-parser-output .ambox-speedy{border-left:10px solid #b32424;background-color:#fee7e6}.mw-parser-output .ambox-delete{border-left:10px solid #b32424}.mw-parser-output .ambox-content{border-left:10px solid #f28500}.mw-parser-output .ambox-style{border-left:10px solid #fc3}.mw-parser-output .ambox-move{border-left:10px solid #9932cc}.mw-parser-output .ambox-protection{border-left:10px solid #a2a9b1}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-text{border:none;padding:0.25em .mbox-text-span{margin-left:23px!important}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .ambox{margin:0 10%}}</style><table class="box-Missing_information plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w.svg"><img alt="Wiki letter w.svg" data-file-height="44" data-file-width="44" decoding="async" height="44" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6c/Wiki_letter_w.svg/44px-Wiki_letter_w.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6c/Wiki_letter_w.svg/66px-Wiki_letter_w.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6c/Wiki_letter_w.svg/88px-Wiki_letter_w.svg.png 2x" width="44"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article <b>is missing information</b> about times and places when exercise was viewed negatively.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please expand the article to include this information. Further details may exist on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Exercise" title="Talk:Exercise">talk page</a>.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2021</span>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Aerobic_exercise#History" title="Aerobic exercise">Aerobic exercise § History</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fitness_culture" title="Fitness culture">Fitness culture</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_physical_training_and_fitness" title="History of physical training and fitness">History of physical training and fitness</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roper%27s_gymnasium,_Philadelphia,_circa_1831.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="467" data-file-width="700" decoding="async" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Roper%27s_gymnasium%2C_Philadelphia%2C_circa_1831.jpg/250px-Roper%27s_gymnasium%2C_Philadelphia%2C_circa_1831.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Roper%27s_gymnasium%2C_Philadelphia%2C_circa_1831.jpg/375px-Roper%27s_gymnasium%2C_Philadelphia%2C_circa_1831.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Roper%27s_gymnasium%2C_Philadelphia%2C_circa_1831.jpg/500px-Roper%27s_gymnasium%2C_Philadelphia%2C_circa_1831.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roper%27s_gymnasium,_Philadelphia,_circa_1831.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Roper's gymnasium, Philadelphia, USA, circa 1831.</div></div></div>
<p>The benefits of exercise have been known since antiquity. Dating back to 65 BCE, it was <a href="/wiki/Cicero" title="Cicero">Marcus Cicero</a>, Roman politician and lawyer, who stated: "It is exercise alone that supports the spirits, and keeps the mind in vigor."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> Exercise was also seen to be valued later in history during the <a href="/wiki/Early_Middle_Ages" title="Early Middle Ages">Early Middle Ages</a> as a means of survival by the <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic peoples</a> of Northern Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup>
</p><p>More recently, exercise was regarded as a beneficial force in the 19th century. In 1858 <a href="/wiki/Archibald_MacLaren" title="Archibald MacLaren">Archibald MacLaren</a> opened a <a href="/wiki/Gym" title="Gym">gymnasium</a> at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">University of Oxford</a> and instituted a training regimen for Major <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Hammersley_(born_1824)" title="Frederick Hammersley (born 1824)">Frederick Hammersley</a> and 12 non-commissioned officers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> This regimen was assimilated into the training of the <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a>, which formed the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Army_Physical_Training_Corps" title="Royal Army Physical Training Corps">Army Gymnastic Staff</a> in 1860 and made sport an important part of military life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> Several mass exercise movements were started in the early twentieth century as well. The first and most significant of these in the UK was the Women's League of Health and Beauty, founded in 1930 by <a href="/wiki/Mary_Bagot_Stack" title="Mary Bagot Stack">Mary Bagot Stack</a>, that had 166,000 members in 1937.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FitnessLeague_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-FitnessLeague-154">[154]</a></sup>
</p><p>The link between physical health and exercise (or lack of it) was further established in 1949 and reported in 1953 by a team led by <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Morris" title="Jerry Morris">Jerry Morris</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morris1953_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-Morris1953-156">[156]</a></sup> Dr. Morris noted that men of similar social class and occupation (bus conductors versus bus drivers) had markedly different rates of heart attacks, depending on the level of exercise they got: bus drivers had a sedentary occupation and a higher incidence of heart disease, while bus conductors were forced to move continually and had a lower incidence of heart disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morris1953_156-1"><a href="#cite_note-Morris1953-156">[156]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_animals">Other animals</span></h2>
<p>Studies of animals indicate that physical activity may be more adaptable than changes in food intake to regulate <a href="/wiki/Energy_homeostasis" title="Energy homeostasis">energy balance</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Mouse" title="Mouse">Mice</a> having access to <a href="/wiki/Hamster_wheel" title="Hamster wheel">activity wheels</a> engaged in voluntary exercise and increased their propensity to run as adults.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Selective_breeding" title="Selective breeding">Artificial selection</a> of mice exhibited significant <a href="/wiki/Heredity" title="Heredity">heritability</a> in voluntary exercise levels,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> with "high-runner" <a href="/wiki/Breed" title="Breed">breeds</a> having enhanced <a href="/wiki/VO2_max" title="VO2 max">aerobic capacity</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hippocampus" title="Hippocampus">hippocampal</a> <a href="/wiki/Neurogenesis" title="Neurogenesis">neurogenesis</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> and skeletal muscle <a href="/wiki/Morphology_(biology)" title="Morphology (biology)">morphology</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup>
</p><p>The effects of exercise training appear to be heterogeneous across non-mammalian species. As examples, exercise training of <a href="/wiki/Salmon" title="Salmon">salmon</a> showed minor improvements of endurance,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> and a forced swimming regimen of <a href="/wiki/Yellowtail_amberjack" title="Yellowtail amberjack">yellowtail amberjack</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rainbow_trout" title="Rainbow trout">rainbow trout</a> accelerated their growth rates and altered muscle morphology favorable for sustained swimming.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Crocodile" title="Crocodile">Crocodiles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alligator" title="Alligator">alligators</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Duck" title="Duck">ducks</a> showed elevated aerobic capacity following exercise training.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Owerk_Baud_2008_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-Owerk_Baud_2008-166">[166]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> No effect of endurance training was found in most studies of lizards,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Owerk_Baud_2008_166-1"><a href="#cite_note-Owerk_Baud_2008-166">[166]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Garland_et_al_1987_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-Garland_et_al_1987-169">[169]</a></sup> although one study did report a training effect.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jeb_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-jeb-170">[170]</a></sup> In lizards, <a href="/wiki/Sprint_(running)" title="Sprint (running)">sprint training</a> had no effect on maximal exercise capacity,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jeb_170-1"><a href="#cite_note-jeb-170">[170]</a></sup> and muscular damage from over-training occurred following weeks of forced treadmill exercise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Garland_et_al_1987_169-1"><a href="#cite_note-Garland_et_al_1987-169">[169]</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_–_neurotrophic_factors_+_basal_ganglia-43"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_–_neurotrophic_factors_+_basal_ganglia_43-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_–_neurotrophic_factors_+_basal_ganglia_43-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFPaillardRollandde_Souto_Barreto2015">Paillard T, Rolland Y, de Souto Barreto P (July 2015). <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4507374" rel="nofollow">"Protective Effects of Physical Exercise in Alzheimer's Disease and Parkinson's Disease: A Narrative Review"</a>. <i>J Clin Neurol</i>. <b>11</b> (3): 212–219. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.3988%2Fjcn.2015.11.3.212" rel="nofollow">10.3988/jcn.2015.11.3.212</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMC_(identifier)" title="PMC (identifier)">PMC</a> <span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4507374" rel="nofollow">4507374</a></span>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/26174783" rel="nofollow">26174783</a>. <q>Aerobic physical exercise (PE) activates the release of neurotrophic factors and promotes angiogenesis, thereby facilitating neurogenesis and synaptogenesis, which in turn improve memory and cognitive functions. ... Exercise limits the alteration in dopaminergic neurons in the substantia nigra and contributes to optimal functioning of the basal ganglia involved in motor commands and control by adaptive mechanisms involving dopamine and glutamate neurotransmission.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=J+Clin+Neurol&amp;rft.atitle=Protective+Effects+of+Physical+Exercise+in+Alzheimer%27s+Disease+and+Parkinson%27s+Disease%3A+A+Narrative+Review&amp;rft.volume=11&amp;rft.issue=3&amp;rft.pages=212-219&amp;rft.date=2015-07&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC4507374%23id-name%3DPMC&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F26174783&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.3988%2Fjcn.2015.11.3.212&amp;rft.aulast=Paillard&amp;rft.aufirst=T&amp;rft.au=Rolland%2C+Y&amp;rft.au=de+Souto+Barreto%2C+P&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC4507374&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AExercise"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Summary_of_effects-44"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Summary_of_effects_44-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Summary_of_effects_44-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFMcKeeDaneshvarAlvarezStein2014">McKee AC, Daneshvar DH, Alvarez VE, Stein TD (January 2014). <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4255282" rel="nofollow">"The neuropathology of sport"</a>. <i>Acta Neuropathol</i>. <b>127</b> (1): 29–51. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1007%2Fs00401-013-1230-6" rel="nofollow">10.1007/s00401-013-1230-6</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMC_(identifier)" title="PMC (identifier)">PMC</a> <span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4255282" rel="nofollow">4255282</a></span>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/24366527" rel="nofollow">24366527</a>. <q>The benefits of regular exercise, physical fitness and sports participation on cardiovascular and brain health are undeniable ... Exercise also enhances psychological health, reduces age-related loss of brain volume, improves cognition, reduces the risk of developing dementia, and impedes neurodegeneration.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Acta+Neuropathol.&amp;rft.atitle=The+neuropathology+of+sport&amp;rft.volume=127&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.pages=29-51&amp;rft.date=2014-01&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC4255282%23id-name%3DPMC&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F24366527&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1007%2Fs00401-013-1230-6&amp;rft.aulast=McKee&amp;rft.aufirst=AC&amp;rft.au=Daneshvar%2C+DH&amp;rft.au=Alvarez%2C+VE&amp;rft.au=Stein%2C+TD&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC4255282&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AExercise"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_epigenome-45"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_epigenome_45-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_epigenome_45-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFDenhamMarquesO'BrienCharchar2014">Denham J, Marques FZ, O'Brien BJ, Charchar FJ (February 2014). "Exercise: putting action into our epigenome". <i>Sports Med</i>. <b>44</b> (2): 189–209. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1007%2Fs40279-013-0114-1" rel="nofollow">10.1007/s40279-013-0114-1</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/24163284" rel="nofollow">24163284</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S2CID_(identifier)" title="S2CID (identifier)">S2CID</a> <a class="external text" href="https://api.semanticscholar.org/CorpusID:30210091" rel="nofollow">30210091</a>. <q>Aerobic physical exercise produces numerous health benefits in the brain. Regular engagement in physical exercise enhances cognitive functioning, increases brain neurotrophic proteins, such as brain-derived neurotrophic factor (BDNF), and prevents cognitive diseases. Recent findings highlight a role for aerobic exercise in modulating chromatin remodelers. ... These results were the first to demonstrate that acute and relatively short aerobic exercise modulates epigenetic modifications. The transient epigenetic modifications observed due to chronic running training have also been associated with improved learning and stress-coping strategies, epigenetic changes and increased c-Fos-positive neurons ... Nonetheless, these studies demonstrate the existence of epigenetic changes after acute and chronic exercise and show they are associated with improved cognitive function and elevated markers of neurotrophic factors and neuronal activity (BDNF and c-Fos). ... The aerobic exercise training-induced changes to miRNA profile in the brain seem to be intensity-dependent. These few studies provide a basis for further exploration into potential miRNAs involved in brain and neuronal development and recovery via aerobic exercise.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Sports+Med&amp;rft.atitle=Exercise%3A+putting+action+into+our+epigenome&amp;rft.volume=44&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.pages=189-209&amp;rft.date=2014-02&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fapi.semanticscholar.org%2FCorpusID%3A30210091%23id-name%3DS2CID&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F24163284&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1007%2Fs40279-013-0114-1&amp;rft.aulast=Denham&amp;rft.aufirst=J&amp;rft.au=Marques%2C+FZ&amp;rft.au=O%27Brien%2C+BJ&amp;rft.au=Charchar%2C+FJ&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AExercise"></span></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_healthy_young_adult_2016_SystRev-51"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_healthy_young_adult_2016_SystRev_51-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_healthy_young_adult_2016_SystRev_51-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_healthy_young_adult_2016_SystRev_51-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFCoxO'DwyerCookVetter2016">Cox EP, O'Dwyer N, Cook R, Vetter M, Cheng HL, Rooney K, O'Connor H (August 2016). "Relationship between physical activity and cognitive function in apparently healthy young to middle-aged adults: A systematic review". <i>J. Sci. Med. Sport</i>. <b>19</b> (8): 616–628. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1016%2Fj.jsams.2015.09.003" rel="nofollow">10.1016/j.jsams.2015.09.003</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/26552574" rel="nofollow">26552574</a>. <q>A range of validated platforms assessed CF across three domains: executive function (12 studies), memory (four studies) and processing speed (seven studies). ... In studies of executive function, five found a significant ES in favour of higher PA, ranging from small to large. Although three of four studies in the memory domain reported a significant benefit of higher PA, there was only one significant ES, which favoured low PA. Only one study examining processing speed had a significant ES, favouring higher PA.<br/>CONCLUSIONS: A limited body of evidence supports a positive effect of PA on CF in young to middle-aged adults. Further research into this relationship at this age stage is warranted. ...<br/>Significant positive effects of PA on cognitive function were found in 12 of the 14 included manuscripts, the relationship being most consistent for executive function, intermediate for memory and weak for processing speed.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=J.+Sci.+Med.+Sport&amp;rft.atitle=Relationship+between+physical+activity+and+cognitive+function+in+apparently+healthy+young+to+middle-aged+adults%3A+A+systematic+review&amp;rft.volume=19&amp;rft.issue=8&amp;rft.pages=616-628&amp;rft.date=2016-08&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1016%2Fj.jsams.2015.09.003&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F26552574&amp;rft.aulast=Cox&amp;rft.aufirst=EP&amp;rft.au=O%27Dwyer%2C+N&amp;rft.au=Cook%2C+R&amp;rft.au=Vetter%2C+M&amp;rft.au=Cheng%2C+HL&amp;rft.au=Rooney%2C+K&amp;rft.au=O%27Connor%2C+H&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AExercise"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Depression_QoL_meta-analysis-52"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Depression_QoL_meta-analysis_52-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Depression_QoL_meta-analysis_52-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Depression_QoL_meta-analysis_52-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFSchuchVancampfortRosenbaumRichards2016">Schuch FB, Vancampfort D, Rosenbaum S, Richards J, Ward PB, Stubbs B (July 2016). <a class="external text" href="https://kclpure.kcl.ac.uk/portal/en/publications/exercise-improves-physical-and-psychological-quality-of-life-in-people-with-depression-a-metaanalysis-including-the-evaluation-of-control-group-response(9d2c5d0c-a5a9-4e46-a763-6b1398bce0f6).html" rel="nofollow">"Exercise improves physical and psychological quality of life in people with depression: A meta-analysis including the evaluation of control group response"</a>. <i>Psychiatry Res</i>. <b>241</b>: 47–54. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1016%2Fj.psychres.2016.04.054" rel="nofollow">10.1016/j.psychres.2016.04.054</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/27155287" rel="nofollow">27155287</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S2CID_(identifier)" title="S2CID (identifier)">S2CID</a> <a class="external text" href="https://api.semanticscholar.org/CorpusID:4787287" rel="nofollow">4787287</a>. <q>Exercise has established efficacy as an antidepressant in people with depression. ... Exercise significantly improved physical and psychological domains and overall QoL. ... The lack of improvement among control groups reinforces the role of exercise as a treatment for depression with benefits to QoL.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Psychiatry+Res.&amp;rft.atitle=Exercise+improves+physical+and+psychological+quality+of+life+in+people+with+depression%3A+A+meta-analysis+including+the+evaluation+of+control+group+response&amp;rft.volume=241&amp;rft.pages=47-54&amp;rft.date=2016-07&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fapi.semanticscholar.org%2FCorpusID%3A4787287%23id-name%3DS2CID&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F27155287&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1016%2Fj.psychres.2016.04.054&amp;rft.aulast=Schuch&amp;rft.aufirst=FB&amp;rft.au=Vancampfort%2C+D&amp;rft.au=Rosenbaum%2C+S&amp;rft.au=Richards%2C+J&amp;rft.au=Ward%2C+PB&amp;rft.au=Stubbs%2C+B&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fkclpure.kcl.ac.uk%2Fportal%2Fen%2Fpublications%2Fexercise-improves-physical-and-psychological-quality-of-life-in-people-with-depression-a-metaanalysis-including-the-evaluation-of-control-group-response%289d2c5d0c-a5a9-4e46-a763-6b1398bce0f6%29.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AExercise"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Aging_QoL_review-53"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Aging_QoL_review_53-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFPrataliMastorciVitielloSironi2014">Pratali L, Mastorci F, Vitiello N, Sironi A, Gastaldelli A, Gemignani A (November 2014). <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4897547" rel="nofollow">"Motor Activity in Aging: An Integrated Approach for Better Quality of Life"</a>. <i>International Scholarly Research Notices</i>. <b>2014</b>: 257248. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1155%2F2014%2F257248" rel="nofollow">10.1155/2014/257248</a></span>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMC_(identifier)" title="PMC (identifier)">PMC</a> <span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4897547" rel="nofollow">4897547</a></span>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/27351018" rel="nofollow">27351018</a>. <q>Research investigating the effects of exercise on older adults has primarily focused on brain structural and functional changes with relation to cognitive improvement. In particular, several cross-sectional and intervention studies have shown a positive association between physical activity and cognition in older persons [86] and an inverse correlation with cognitive decline and dementia [87]. Older adults enrolled in a 6-month aerobic fitness intervention increased brain volume in both gray matter (anterior cingulate cortex, supplementary motor area, posterior middle frontal gyrus, and left superior temporal lobe) and white matter (anterior third of corpus callosum) [88]. In addition, Colcombe and colleagues showed that older adults with higher cardiovascular fitness levels are better at activating attentional resources, including decreased activation of the anterior cingulated cortex. One of the possible mechanisms by which physical activity may benefit cognition is that physical activity maintains brain plasticity, increases brain volume, stimulates neurogenesis and synaptogenesis, and increases neurotrophic factors in different areas of the brain, possibly providing reserve against later cognitive decline and dementia [89, 90].</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=International+Scholarly+Research+Notices&amp;rft.atitle=Motor+Activity+in+Aging%3A+An+Integrated+Approach+for+Better+Quality+of+Life&amp;rft.volume=2014&amp;rft.pages=257248&amp;rft.date=2014-11&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC4897547%23id-name%3DPMC&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F27351018&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1155%2F2014%2F257248&amp;rft.aulast=Pratali&amp;rft.aufirst=L&amp;rft.au=Mastorci%2C+F&amp;rft.au=Vitiello%2C+N&amp;rft.au=Sironi%2C+A&amp;rft.au=Gastaldelli%2C+A&amp;rft.au=Gemignani%2C+A&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC4897547&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AExercise"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-54"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-54">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFMandolesiPolverinoMontuoriFoti2018">Mandolesi, Laura; Polverino, Arianna; Montuori, Simone; Foti, Francesca; Ferraioli, Giampaolo; Sorrentino, Pierpaolo; Sorrentino, Giuseppe (27 April 2018). <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC5934999" rel="nofollow">"Effects of Physical Exercise on Cognitive Functioning and Wellbeing: Biological and Psychological Benefits"</a>. <i>Frontiers in Psychology</i>. <b>9</b>: 509. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.3389%2Ffpsyg.2018.00509" rel="nofollow">10.3389/fpsyg.2018.00509</a></span>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMC_(identifier)" title="PMC (identifier)">PMC</a> <span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC5934999" rel="nofollow">5934999</a></span>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/29755380" rel="nofollow">29755380</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Frontiers+in+Psychology&amp;rft.atitle=Effects+of+Physical+Exercise+on+Cognitive+Functioning+and+Wellbeing%3A+Biological+and+Psychological+Benefits&amp;rft.volume=9&amp;rft.pages=509&amp;rft.date=2018-04-27&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC5934999%23id-name%3DPMC&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F29755380&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.3389%2Ffpsyg.2018.00509&amp;rft.aulast=Mandolesi&amp;rft.aufirst=Laura&amp;rft.au=Polverino%2C+Arianna&amp;rft.au=Montuori%2C+Simone&amp;rft.au=Foti%2C+Francesca&amp;rft.au=Ferraioli%2C+Giampaolo&amp;rft.au=Sorrentino%2C+Pierpaolo&amp;rft.au=Sorrentino%2C+Giuseppe&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC5934999&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AExercise"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Neurobiological_effects_of_acute_exercise_–_2017_review-55"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Neurobiological_effects_of_acute_exercise_–_2017_review_55-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Neurobiological_effects_of_acute_exercise_–_2017_review_55-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Neurobiological_effects_of_acute_exercise_–_2017_review_55-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Neurobiological_effects_of_acute_exercise_–_2017_review_55-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFBasso_JC,_Suzuki_WA2017">Basso JC, Suzuki WA (March 2017). <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC5928534" rel="nofollow">"The Effects of Acute Exercise on Mood, Cognition, Neurophysiology, and Neurochemical Pathways: A Review"</a>. <i>Brain Plasticity</i>. <b>2</b> (2): 127–152. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.3233%2FBPL-160040" rel="nofollow">10.3233/BPL-160040</a></span>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMC_(identifier)" title="PMC (identifier)">PMC</a> <span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC5928534" rel="nofollow">5928534</a></span>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/29765853" rel="nofollow">29765853</a>. <q>A large collection of research in humans has shown that a single bout of exercise alters behavior at the level of affective state and cognitive functioning in several key ways. In terms of affective state, acute exercise decreases negative affect, increases positive affect, and decreases the psychological and physiological response to acute stress. These effects have been reported to persist for up to 24 hours after exercise cessation. In terms of cognitive functioning, acute exercise primarily enhances executive functions dependent on the prefrontal cortex including attention, working memory, problem solving, cognitive flexibility, verbal fluency, decision making, and inhibitory control. These positive changes have been demonstrated to occur with very low to very high exercise intensities, with effects lasting for up to two hours after the end of the exercise bout (Fig. 1A). Moreover, many of these neuropsychological assessments measure several aspects of behavior including both accuracy of performance and speed of processing. McMorris and Hale performed a meta-analysis examining the effects of acute exercise on both accuracy and speed of processing, revealing that speed significantly improved post-exercise, with minimal or no effect on accuracy. These authors concluded that increasing task difficulty or complexity may help to augment the effect of acute exercise on accuracy. ... However, in a comprehensive meta-analysis, Chang and colleagues found that exercise intensities ranging from very light (&lt;50% MHR) to very hard (&gt;93% MHR) have all been reported to improve cognitive functioning.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Brain+Plasticity&amp;rft.atitle=The+Effects+of+Acute+Exercise+on+Mood%2C+Cognition%2C+Neurophysiology%2C+and+Neurochemical+Pathways%3A+A+Review&amp;rft.volume=2&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.pages=127-152&amp;rft.date=2017-03&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC5928534%23id-name%3DPMC&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F29765853&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.3233%2FBPL-160040&amp;rft.au=Basso+JC%2C+Suzuki+WA&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC5928534&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AExercise"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Euphoria_review-56"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Euphoria_review_56-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1 cs1-prop-foreign-lang-source" id="CITEREFCunhaRibeiroOliveira2008">Cunha GS, Ribeiro JL, Oliveira AR (June 2008). <a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1590%2FS0004-27302008000400004" rel="nofollow">"[Levels of beta-endorphin in response to exercise and overtraining]"</a>. <i>Arq Bras Endocrinol Metabol</i> (in Portuguese). <b>52</b> (4): 589–598. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1590%2FS0004-27302008000400004" rel="nofollow">10.1590/S0004-27302008000400004</a></span>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/18604371" rel="nofollow">18604371</a>. <q>Interestingly, some symptoms of OT are related to beta-endorphin (beta-end(1-31)) effects. Some of its effects, such as analgesia, increasing lactate tolerance, and exercise-induced euphoria, are important for training.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Arq+Bras+Endocrinol+Metabol&amp;rft.atitle=%5BLevels+of+beta-endorphin+in+response+to+exercise+and+overtraining%5D&amp;rft.volume=52&amp;rft.issue=4&amp;rft.pages=589-598&amp;rft.date=2008-06&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1590%2FS0004-27302008000400004&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F18604371&amp;rft.aulast=Cunha&amp;rft.aufirst=GS&amp;rft.au=Ribeiro%2C+JL&amp;rft.au=Oliveira%2C+AR&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fdoi.org%2F10.1590%252FS0004-27302008000400004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AExercise"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Runner-57"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Runner_57-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFBoeckerSprengerSpilkerHenriksen2008">Boecker H, Sprenger T, Spilker ME, Henriksen G, Koppenhoefer M, Wagner KJ, Valet M, Berthele A, Tolle TR (2008). <a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1093%2Fcercor%2Fbhn013" rel="nofollow">"The runner's high: opioidergic mechanisms in the human brain"</a>. <i>Cereb. <li id="cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_depression_intervention-58"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_depression_intervention_58-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_depression_intervention_58-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_depression_intervention_58-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_depression_intervention_58-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFJosefssonLindwallArcher2014">Josefsson T, Lindwall M, Archer T (2014). <li id="cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Physical_activity_intervention-59"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Physical_activity_intervention_59-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Physical_activity_intervention_59-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Physical_activity_intervention_59-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFRosenbaumTiedemannSherringtonCurtis2014">Rosenbaum S, Tiedemann A, Sherrington C, Curtis J, Ward PB (2014). "Physical activity interventions for people with mental illness: a systematic review and meta-analysis". <i>J Clin Psychiatry</i>. <b>75</b> (9): 964–974. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.4088%2FJCP.13r08765" rel="nofollow">10.4088/JCP.13r08765</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/24813261" rel="nofollow">24813261</a>. <q>This systematic review and meta-analysis found that physical activity reduced depressive symptoms among people with a psychiatric illness.  The current meta-analysis differs from previous studies, as it included participants with depressive symptoms with a variety of psychiatric diagnoses (except dysthymia and eating disorders). ... This review provides strong evidence for the antidepressant effect of physical activity; however, the optimal exercise modality, volume, and intensity remain to be determined. ... Few interventions exist whereby patients can hope to achieve improvements in both psychiatric symptoms and physical health simultaneously without significant risks of adverse effects. Physical activity offers substantial promise for improving outcomes for people living with mental illness, and the inclusion of physical activity and exercise programs within treatment facilities is warranted given the results of this review.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=J+Clin+Psychiatry&amp;rft.atitle=Physical+activity+interventions+for+people+with+mental+illness%3A+a+systematic+review+and+meta-analysis&amp;rft.volume=75&amp;rft.issue=9&amp;rft.pages=964-974&amp;rft.date=2014&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.4088%2FJCP.13r08765&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F24813261&amp;rft.aulast=Rosenbaum&amp;rft.aufirst=S&amp;rft.au=Tiedemann%2C+A&amp;rft.au=Sherrington%2C+C&amp;rft.au=Curtis%2C+J&amp;rft.au=Ward%2C+PB&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AExercise"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_BDNF_meta_analysis-60"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_BDNF_meta_analysis_60-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFSzuhanyBugattiOtto2014">Szuhany KL, Bugatti M, Otto MW (October 2014). <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4314337" rel="nofollow">"A meta-analytic review of the effects of exercise on brain-derived neurotrophic factor"</a>. <i>J Psychiatr Res</i>. <b>60C</b>: 56–64. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1016%2Fj.jpsychires.2014.10.003" rel="nofollow">10.1016/j.jpsychires.2014.10.003</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMC_(identifier)" title="PMC (identifier)">PMC</a> <span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4314337" rel="nofollow">4314337</a></span>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/25455510" rel="nofollow">25455510</a>. <q>Consistent evidence indicates that exercise improves cognition and mood, with preliminary evidence suggesting that brain-derived neurotrophic factor (BDNF) may mediate these effects. The aim of the current meta-analysis was to provide an estimate of the strength of the association between exercise and increased BDNF levels in humans across multiple exercise paradigms. We conducted a meta-analysis of 29 studies (N = 1111 participants) examining the effect of exercise on BDNF levels in three exercise paradigms: (1) a single session of exercise, (2) a session of exercise following a program of regular exercise, and (3) resting BDNF levels following a program of regular exercise. Moderators of this effect were also examined. Results demonstrated a moderate effect size for increases in BDNF following a single session of exercise (Hedges' g = 0.46, p &lt; 0.001). Further, regular exercise intensified the effect of a session of exercise on BDNF levels (Hedges' g = 0.59, p = 0.02). Finally, results indicated a small effect of regular exercise on resting BDNF levels (Hedges' g = 0.27, p = 0.005). ... Effect size analysis supports the role of exercise as a strategy for enhancing BDNF activity in humans.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=J+Psychiatr+Res&amp;rft.atitle=A+meta-analytic+review+of+the+effects+of+exercise+on+brain-derived+neurotrophic+factor&amp;rft.volume=60C&amp;rft.pages=56-64&amp;rft.date=2014-10&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC4314337%23id-name%3DPMC&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F25455510&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1016%2Fj.jpsychires.2014.10.003&amp;rft.aulast=Szuhany&amp;rft.aufirst=KL&amp;rft.au=Bugatti%2C+M&amp;rft.au=Otto%2C+MW&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC4314337&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AExercise"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_children-61"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_children_61-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFLeesHopkins2013">Lees C, Hopkins J (2013). <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC3809922" rel="nofollow">"Effect of aerobic exercise on cognition, academic achievement, and psychosocial function in children: a systematic review of randomized control trials"</a>. <i>Prev Chronic Dis</i>. <b>10</b>: E174. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.5888%2Fpcd10.130010" rel="nofollow">10.5888/pcd10.130010</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMC_(identifier)" title="PMC (identifier)">PMC</a> <span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC3809922" rel="nofollow">3809922</a></span>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/24157077" rel="nofollow">24157077</a>. <q>This omission is relevant, given the evidence that aerobic-based physical activity generates structural changes in the brain, such as neurogenesis, angiogenesis, increased hippocampal volume, and connectivity (12,13). In children, a positive relationship between aerobic fitness, hippocampal volume, and memory has been found (12,13). ... Mental health outcomes included reduced depression and increased self-esteem, although no change was found in anxiety levels (18). ... This systematic review of the literature found that [aerobic physical activity (APA)] is positively associated with cognition, academic achievement, behavior, and psychosocial functioning outcomes. Importantly, Shephard also showed that curriculum time reassigned to APA still results in a measurable, albeit small, improvement in academic performance (24).  ... The actual aerobic-based activity does not appear to be a major factor; interventions used many different types of APA and found similar associations. In positive association studies, intensity of the aerobic activity was moderate to vigorous. The amount of time spent in APA varied significantly between studies; however, even as little as 45 minutes per week appeared to have a benefit.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Prev+Chronic+Dis&amp;rft.atitle=Effect+of+aerobic+exercise+on+cognition%2C+academic+achievement%2C+and+psychosocial+function+in+children%3A+a+systematic+review+of+randomized+control+trials&amp;rft.volume=10&amp;rft.pages=E174&amp;rft.date=2013&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC3809922%23id-name%3DPMC&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F24157077&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.5888%2Fpcd10.130010&amp;rft.aulast=Lees&amp;rft.aufirst=C&amp;rft.au=Hopkins%2C+J&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC3809922&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AExercise"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_MDD_antidepressant-62"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_MDD_antidepressant_62-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_MDD_antidepressant_62-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_MDD_antidepressant_62-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Exercise_MDD_antidepressant_62-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFMuraMoroPattenCarta2014">Mura G, Moro MF, Patten SB, Carta MG (2014). "Exercise as an add-on strategy for the treatment of major depressive disorder: a systematic review". <i>CNS Spectr</i>. <b>19</b> (6): 496–508. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1017%2FS1092852913000953" rel="nofollow">10.1017/S1092852913000953</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/24589012" rel="nofollow">24589012</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S2CID_(identifier)" title="S2CID (identifier)">S2CID</a> <a class="external text" href="https://api.semanticscholar.org/CorpusID:32304140" rel="nofollow">32304140</a>. <q>Considered overall, the studies included in the present review showed a strong effectiveness of exercise combined with antidepressants. ...<br/>Conclusions<br/> This is the first review to have focused on exercise as an add-on strategy in the treatment of MDD. Our findings corroborate some previous observations that were based on few studies and which were difficult to generalize. Given the results of the present article, it seems that exercise might be an effective strategy to enhance the antidepressant effect of medication treatments. Moreover, we hypothesize that the main role of exercise on treatment-resistant depression is in inducing neurogenesis by increasing BDNF expression, as was demonstrated by several recent studies.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=CNS+Spectr&amp;rft.atitle=Exercise+as+an+add-on+strategy+for+the+treatment+of+major+depressive+disorder%3A+a+systematic+review&amp;rft.volume=19&amp;rft.issue=6&amp;rft.pages=496-508&amp;rft.date=2014&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fapi.semanticscholar.org%2FCorpusID%3A32304140%23id-name%3DS2CID&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F24589012&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1017%2FS1092852913000953&amp;rft.aulast=Mura&amp;rft.aufirst=G&amp;rft.au=Moro%2C+MF&amp;rft.au=Patten%2C+SB&amp;rft.au=Carta%2C+MG&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AExercise"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_ADHD_exercise_2016_SystRev-63"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_ADHD_exercise_2016_SystRev_63-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFDen_HeijerGroenTuchaFuermaier2016">Den Heijer AE, Groen Y, Tucha L, Fuermaier AB, Koerts J, Lange KW, Thome J, Tucha O (July 2016). <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC5281644" rel="nofollow">"Sweat it out? The effects of physical exercise on cognition and behavior in children and adults with ADHD: a systematic literature review"</a>. <i>J. Neural Transm. (Vienna)</i>. <b>124</b> (Suppl 1): 3–26. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1007%2Fs00702-016-1593-7" rel="nofollow">10.1007/s00702-016-1593-7</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMC_(identifier)" title="PMC (identifier)">PMC</a> <span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC5281644" rel="nofollow">5281644</a></span>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/27400928" rel="nofollow">27400928</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=J.+Neural+Transm.+%28Vienna%29&amp;rft.atitle=Sweat+it+out%3F+The+effects+of+physical+exercise+on+cognition+and+behavior+in+children+and+adults+with+ADHD%3A+a+systematic+literature+review&amp;rft.volume=124&amp;rft.issue=Suppl+1&amp;rft.pages=3-26&amp;rft.date=2016-07&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC5281644%23id-name%3DPMC&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F27400928&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1007%2Fs00702-016-1593-7&amp;rft.aulast=Den+Heijer&amp;rft.aufirst=AE&amp;rft.au=Groen%2C+Y&amp;rft.au=Tucha%2C+L&amp;rft.au=Fuermaier%2C+AB&amp;rft.au=Koerts%2C+J&amp;rft.au=Lange%2C+KW&amp;rft.au=Thome%2C+J&amp;rft.au=Tucha%2C+O&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC5281644&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AExercise"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_ADHD_Exercise_2014-64"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_ADHD_Exercise_2014_64-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFKampSperlichHolmberg2014">Kamp CF, Sperlich B, Holmberg HC (July 2014). <a class="external text" href="http://urn.kb.se/resolve?urn=urn:nbn:se:miun:diva-22594" rel="nofollow">"Exercise reduces the symptoms of attention-deficit/hyperactivity disorder and improves social behaviour, motor skills, strength and neuropsychological parameters"</a>. <i>Acta Paediatr</i>. <b>103</b> (7): 709–14. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1111%2Fapa.12628" rel="nofollow">10.1111/apa.12628</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/24612421" rel="nofollow">24612421</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S2CID_(identifier)" title="S2CID (identifier)">S2CID</a> <a class="external text" href="https://api.semanticscholar.org/CorpusID:45881887" rel="nofollow">45881887</a>. <q>The present review summarises the impact of exercise interventions (1–10 weeks in duration with at least two sessions each week) on parameters related to ADHD in 7-to 13-year-old children. We may conclude that all different types of exercise (here <a href="/wiki/Modern_yoga" title="Modern yoga">yoga</a>, active games with and without the involvement of balls, walking and athletic training) attenuate the characteristic symptoms of ADHD and improve social behaviour, motor skills, strength and neuropsychological parameters without any undesirable side effects. Available reports do not reveal which type, intensity, duration and frequency of exercise is most effective in this respect and future research focusing on this question with randomised and controlled long-term interventions is warranted.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Acta+Paediatr.&amp;rft.atitle=Exercise+reduces+the+symptoms+of+attention-deficit%2Fhyperactivity+disorder+and+improves+social+behaviour%2C+motor+skills%2C+strength+and+neuropsychological+parameters&amp;rft.volume=103&amp;rft.issue=7&amp;rft.pages=709-14&amp;rft.date=2014-07&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fapi.semanticscholar.org%2FCorpusID%3A45881887%23id-name%3DS2CID&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F24612421&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1111%2Fapa.12628&amp;rft.aulast=Kamp&amp;rft.aufirst=CF&amp;rft.au=Sperlich%2C+B&amp;rft.au=Holmberg%2C+HC&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Furn.kb.se%2Fresolve%3Furn%3Durn%3Anbn%3Ase%3Amiun%3Adiva-22594&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AExercise"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_December_2017_AAN_Clinical_Practice_Guideline_for_MCI-65"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_December_2017_AAN_Clinical_Practice_Guideline_for_MCI_65-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFPetersenLopezArmstrongGetchius2018">Petersen RC, Lopez O, Armstrong MJ, Getchius T, Ganguli M, Gloss D, Gronseth GS, Marson D, Pringsheim T, Day GS, Sager M, Stevens J, Rae-Grant A (January 2018). <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC5772157" rel="nofollow">"Practice guideline update summary: Mild cognitive impairment – Report of the Guideline Development, Dissemination, and Implementation Subcommittee of the American Academy of Neurology"</a>. <i>Neurology</i>. Special article. <b>90</b> (3): 126–135. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1212%2FWNL.0000000000004826" rel="nofollow">10.1212/WNL.0000000000004826</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMC_(identifier)" title="PMC (identifier)">PMC</a> <span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC5772157" rel="nofollow">5772157</a></span>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/29282327" rel="nofollow">29282327</a>. <q>In patients with MCI, exercise training (6 months) is likely to improve cognitive measures and cognitive training may improve cognitive measures. ... Clinicians should recommend regular exercise (Level B). ... For patients diagnosed with MCI, clinicians should recommend regular exercise (twice/week) as part of an overall approach to management (Level B).</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Neurology&amp;rft.atitle=Practice+guideline+update+summary%3A+Mild+cognitive+impairment+%E2%80%93+Report+of+the+Guideline+Development%2C+Dissemination%2C+and+Implementation+Subcommittee+of+the+American+Academy+of+Neurology&amp;rft.volume=90&amp;rft.issue=3&amp;rft.pages=126-135&amp;rft.date=2018-01&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC5772157%23id-name%3DPMC&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F29282327&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1212%2FWNL.0000000000004826&amp;rft.aulast=Petersen&amp;rft.aufirst=RC&amp;rft.au=Lopez%2C+O&amp;rft.au=Armstrong%2C+MJ&amp;rft.au=Getchius%2C+T&amp;rft.au=Ganguli%2C+M&amp;rft.au=Gloss%2C+D&amp;rft.au=Gronseth%2C+GS&amp;rft.au=Marson%2C+D&amp;rft.au=Pringsheim%2C+T&amp;rft.au=Day%2C+GS&amp;rft.au=Sager%2C+M&amp;rft.au=Stevens%2C+J&amp;rft.au=Rae-Grant%2C+A&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC5772157&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AExercise"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Alz_1-66"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Alz_1_66-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFFarinaRustedTabet2014">Farina N, Rusted J, Tabet N (January 2014). "The effect of exercise interventions on cognitive outcome in Alzheimer's disease: a systematic review". <i>Int Psychogeriatr</i>. <b>26</b> (1): 9–18. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1017%2FS1041610213001385" rel="nofollow">10.1017/S1041610213001385</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/23962667" rel="nofollow">23962667</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S2CID_(identifier)" title="S2CID (identifier)">S2CID</a> <a class="external text" href="https://api.semanticscholar.org/CorpusID:24936334" rel="nofollow">24936334</a>. <q>Six RCTs were identified that exclusively considered the effect of exercise in AD patients. Exercise generally had a positive effect on rate of cognitive decline in AD. A meta-analysis found that exercise interventions have a positive effect on global cognitive function, 0.75 (95% CI = 0.32–1.17). ... The most prevalent subtype of dementia is Alzheimer's disease (AD), accounting for up to 65.0% of all dementia cases ... Cognitive decline in AD is attributable at least in part to the buildup of amyloid and tau proteins, which promote neuronal dysfunction and death (Hardy and Selkoe, 2002; Karran et al., 2011). Evidence in transgenic mouse models of AD, in which the mice have artificially elevated amyloid load, suggests that exercise programs are able to improve cognitive function (Adlard et al., 2005; Nichol et al., 2007). Adlard and colleagues also determined that the improvement in cognitive performance occurred in conjunction with a reduced amyloid load. Research that includes direct indices of change in such biomarkers will help to determine the mechanisms by which exercise may act on cognition in AD.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Int+Psychogeriatr&amp;rft.atitle=The+effect+of+exercise+interventions+on+cognitive+outcome+in+Alzheimer%27s+disease%3A+a+systematic+review&amp;rft.volume=26&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.pages=9-18&amp;rft.date=2014-01&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fapi.semanticscholar.org%2FCorpusID%3A24936334%23id-name%3DS2CID&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F23962667&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1017%2FS1041610213001385&amp;rft.aulast=Farina&amp;rft.aufirst=N&amp;rft.au=Rusted%2C+J&amp;rft.au=Tabet%2C+N&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AExercise"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Alz_2-67"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Alz_2_67-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFRaoChouBursleySmulofsky2014">Rao AK, Chou A, Bursley B, Smulofsky J, Jezequel J (January 2014). <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC5360200" rel="nofollow">"Systematic review of the effects of exercise on activities of daily living in people with Alzheimer's disease"</a>. <i>Am J Occup Ther</i>. <b>68</b> (1): 50–56. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.5014%2Fajot.2014.009035" rel="nofollow">10.5014/ajot.2014.009035</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMC_(identifier)" title="PMC (identifier)">PMC</a> <span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC5360200" rel="nofollow">5360200</a></span>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/24367955" rel="nofollow">24367955</a>. <q>Alzheimer's disease (AD) is a progressive neurological disorder characterized by loss in cognitive function, abnormal behavior, and decreased ability to perform basic activities of daily living [(ADLs)] ... All studies included people with AD who completed an exercise program consisting of aerobic, strength, or balance training or any combination of the three. The length of the exercise programs varied from 12 weeks to 12 months. ... Six studies involving 446 participants tested the effect of exercise on ADL performance ... exercise had a large and significant effect on ADL performance (z = 4.07, p &lt; .0001; average effect size = 0.80). ... These positive effects were apparent with programs ranging in length from 12 wk (Santana-Sosa et al., 2008; Teri et al., 2003) and intermediate length of 16 wk (Roach et al., 2011; Vreugdenhil et al., 2012) to 6 mo (Venturelli et al., 2011) and 12 mo (Rolland et al., 2007). Furthermore, the positive effects of a 3-mo intervention lasted 24 mo (Teri et al., 2003). ... No adverse effects of exercise on ADL performance were noted. ... The study with the largest effect size implemented a walking and aerobic program of only 30 min four times a week (Venturelli et al., 2011).</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Am+J+Occup+Ther&amp;rft.atitle=Systematic+review+of+the+effects+of+exercise+on+activities+of+daily+living+in+people+with+Alzheimer%27s+disease&amp;rft.volume=68&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.pages=50-56&amp;rft.date=2014-01&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC5360200%23id-name%3DPMC&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F24367955&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.5014%2Fajot.2014.009035&amp;rft.aulast=Rao&amp;rft.aufirst=AK&amp;rft.au=Chou%2C+A&amp;rft.au=Bursley%2C+B&amp;rft.au=Smulofsky%2C+J&amp;rft.au=Jezequel%2C+J&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC5360200&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AExercise"></span></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-Neurobiological_effects_of_physical_exercise_Parkinson_physiotherapy_Cochrane-71"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFTomlinsonPatelMeekHerd2013">Tomlinson CL, Patel S, Meek C, Herd CP, Clarke CE, Stowe R, Shah L, Sackley CM, Deane KH,
